The Complete Real Definition: Scope and Objection
Author defines complete real definition and addresses an objection about its scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the complete real definition (hadd tamm haqiqi) and defend its applicability to composite quiddities using the author's classification argument.

Core Idea
The complete real definition can include composites if redefined as indication by all essentials.

The complete real definition is traditionally defined as 'statement indicating quiddity by genus and differentia.' But this seems to only fit simple essences like 'human'. What about composites like 'black'? The author raises an objection and then resolves it by showing that composites, when defined by all their essential parts, still qualify as complete real definitions—just with a broader definition. Let's walk through his reasoning to see how he saves the classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the standard definition
Find the initial statement that defines 'hadd tamm haqiqi' as 'the statement indicating the quiddity of a thing by its genus and differentia.' Note that this definition assumes the thing has a genus and differentia, i.e., a simple essence.
2
Pinpoint the objection
The objection argues that genus and differentia are only for simple realities; composite realities like colors (black, white) do not have proper genera or differentia. Locate the sentence where the objection is raised.
The objection starts with 'ويتجه عليه أن يقال'.
3
Follow the classification argument
The author argues that definitions of composites (by all their essentials) cannot be descriptions (rasm) because descriptions use accidents or a mix; nor can they be incomplete definitions (hadd naqis) because those do not indicate the complete quiddity. Therefore, they must be complete real definitions. Trace the elimination process.
The categories are: definition (حد), description (رسم), and verbal definition (لفظي).
4
Understand the resolution
The author concedes that the original definition was meant for simple realities, but redefines the complete real definition more broadly: 'the statement indicating the complete quiddity inquired about by its essentials without departing from correspondence and implication.' This covers both simple and composite quiddities.
The new definition is: 'القول الدال على كمال الماهية المسؤول عنها بذاتياتها'.
5
Apply to Islamic sciences
Consider the definition of 'prayer (salat)' in fiqh: 'specific words and actions beginning with takbir and ending with taslim, with intention.' Identify its essential parts (niyyah, takbir, qira'ah, ruku', sujud, etc.) and see how it qualifies as a complete real definition according to the broadened definition.
This definition includes all essential parts and excludes non-essentials.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما كيفية تأليفهما فنقول: أما الحد فينقسم إلى تام حقيقي وإلى ناقص. أما الحد التام الحقيقي فقد قيل فيه أنه القول الدال على ماهية الشيء بجنسه وفصله. ويتجه عليه أن يقال: الجنس والفصل إنما هو خاصة لحدود الحقائق البسيطة، إذ الحقائق المركبة كالأسود والأبيض من حيث هو كذلك، وإن كانت مؤلفة من ذاتيات فليس بأجناس ولا فصول كما عرف. وعند هذا فالأقوال الدالة عليها يبعد أن لا تكون من الأقوال الشارحة مع دلالتها عليها بذاتياتها وإن كانت منها، فإما أن تكون الحدود أو الرسميات أو اللفظيات، لا جائز أن يكون من الرسوم لدلالتها على كمال الماهية المسؤول عنها بذاتياتها، والرسم إنما يدل بالذاتيات والعرضيات أو العرضيات فقط، فلم يبق إلا أن يكون من الحدود وليست من الحدود الناقصة، إذ الحد الناقص ما يميز الذات تمييزاً ذاتياً من غير دلالة على كمال الماهية المشتركة، وما مثل هذه الحدود فدالة على كمال الماهية بجميع ذاتياتها، فلم يبق إلا أن يكون من الحدود التامة الحقيقية، إذ ليس وراء هذه الأقسام قسم آخر له مدخل في الأقوال الشارحة باعتراف صاحب هذا الرسم وهو أفضل المتأخرين، ولا مخلص منه إلا أن يقول إن المراد بالحد المذكور إنما هو الحد الحقيقي الخاص بالحقائق البسيطة، وإن لم يكن ذلك ظاهراً من لفظه، وأما رسمه على وجه يتناول الحدود الحقيقية للماهيات البسيطة والمركبة، فهو أن يقال هو القول الدال على كمال الماهية المسؤول عنها بذاتياتها من غير خروج له عن دلالة المطابقة والتضمن
As for the manner of their composition, we say: The definition is divided into complete real and incomplete. As for the complete real definition, it has been said that it is the statement indicating the quiddity of a thing by its genus and differentia. An objection may be directed at it: genus and differentia are specific to definitions of simple realities, because composite realities like black and white as such, even if composed of essentials, do not have genera or species as is known. Hence the statements indicating them are far from not being among explanatory statements while indicating them by their essentials despite being from them. So they must be either definitions or descriptions or verbal definitions. It is impossible that they be from descriptions because they indicate the complete quiddity inquired about by its essentials, whereas description indicates only by essentials and accidents or by accidents alone. So nothing remains except that they be from definitions, and they are not from incomplete definitions, because the incomplete definition is that which distinguishes the essence by an essential distinction without indicating the complete common quiddity, whereas such definitions indicate the complete quiddity by all its essentials. So nothing remains except that they be from complete real definitions, because there is no other division beyond these that has entry into explanatory statements according to the author of this diagram, who is the best of the later scholars. There is no escape from this except to say that what is meant by the mentioned definition is the real definition specific to simple realities, even if that is not apparent from his wording. As for its definition in a way that encompasses the real definitions of both simple and composite quiddities, it is to say: it is the statement indicating the complete quiddity inquired about by its essentials without departing from the indication of correspondence and implication.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage defines the complete real definition and defends its scope against an objection. The author begins by stating that definition is divided into complete real and incomplete. The complete real definition is said to be the statement that indicates the quiddity of a thing by its genus and differentia. An objection is then raised: genus and differentia are only applicable to simple realities, because composite realities like 'black' or 'white' do not have true genera or species; their essences are composed but not of genera and differentia in the technical sense. The author then argues that despite this, the statements that indicate such composite realities by their essentials cannot be other than explanatory statements. They cannot be descriptions (rasm) because descriptions use accidents or a mix of essentials and accidents, whereas these statements indicate the complete quiddity by all essentials. They cannot be incomplete definitions because incomplete definitions do not indicate the complete quiddity. Therefore, they must be complete real definitions, albeit with a nuance. The only way out is to specify that the definition of complete real definition originally given is meant only for simple realities, and for composite realities a broader definition is needed: a statement indicating the complete quiddity by all its essentials without departing from literal and implicative indication. This passage is explanatory and uses logical reasoning to defend the classification. An example from fiqh: the definition of 'prayer' (salat) as 'specific words and actions beginning with takbir and ending with taslim' — this is a complete definition that includes its essential components. However, the text's own example of 'black' and 'white' shows composite color concepts.

Resolving the Infinite Regress Objection in Defining 'Definition'
Author presents objection that defining 'definition' leads to infinite regress and gives a rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute the claim that defining a universal term leads to an infinite regress by applying the principle that a definition covers itself.

Core Idea
Definition of definition is possible without regress because a universal definition includes itself.

In this passage, the author presents an objection to the very project of defining 'definition'. The objection claims that any definition of 'definition' would require another definition, leading to an endless chain. The author then gives a rebuttal from a qualified scholar, using the example of defining 'even number'. This lesson guides you through understanding and applying this meta-logical principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Find the conditional statement: if we define definition, then that definition itself must be a definition, requiring another definition, ad infinitum. This is an argument from infinite regress.
2
Understand the rebuttal
The qualified scholar argues that when we define 'absolute definition', the definition of the definition of definition is included in it. Any particular definition, insofar as it is a definition, does not need to be defined again because the universal definition covers it.
3
Analyze the analogy
Consider the definition of 'even number' as 'that which is divisible into two equal parts'. This definition covers all even numbers, including any specific even number (like the one in Zayd's hand). Similarly, the definition of 'definition' covers all definitions, including itself.
The analogy shows that universal definitions are self-inclusive without regress.
4
Evaluate the author's critique
The author notes that the inclusion is only insofar as it is a definition, not absolutely. This means the self-inclusivity is limited to the conceptual aspect, which may need further examination.
The text cuts off before the full critique, but this highlights a nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: هذا تعريف الحد بالحد وتعريف الحد بالحد مما يُفضي إلى المحال، فيكون محالاً. بيان أنه يُفضي إلى محال أنه يلزم منه أن يكون للحد حد، ولو كان للحد حد لكان لحد حد الحد حد وهلم جرا إلى ما لا نهاية له وهو محال وما يفضي إلى المحال فهو محال. قال بعض الحذاق: نحن إذا حددنا الحد المطلق فقد دخل فيه حد حدِ الحد، وكل ما يفرض من الحدود من جهة أنه حد فلا يفتقر إلى تحديده ثانياً، وذلك على نحو تحديدنا للزوج بأنه المنقسم بمتساويين في تناوله للزوج الذي في يد زيد وعمرو ونحوه. وفيه نظر: فإنه وإن تناوله فليس إلا من جهة كونه حداً، إما مطلقاً، إذ حد حد
For it was said: This is a definition of definition by definition, and defining definition by definition leads to absurdity, so it is absurd. The explanation that it leads to absurdity is that it necessitates that definition has a definition, and if definition had a definition, then definition of definition would have a definition, and so on ad infinitum, which is absurd, and what leads to absurdity is absurd. Some qualified scholar said: When we define absolute definition, the definition of the definition of definition is included in it, and every assumed definition, insofar as it is a definition, does not need to be defined a second time. This is akin to our definition of 'even number' as 'that which is divisible into two equal parts' covering the even number in Zayd's hand and 'Amr's and so on. There is a point of consideration: for even though it includes it, it is only insofar as it is a definition, either absolutely; because the definition of definition...
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the project of defining 'definition' itself, claiming it leads to infinite regress. The objection is that if we define 'definition', then that definition itself must be a definition, thus requiring a definition of that definition, and so on infinitely — which is absurd. The response from a qualified scholar is that when we define 'absolute definition', the definition of the definition of definition is implicitly included, and any particular definition, insofar as it is a definition, does not require a second definition. He analogizes to defining 'even number' as something divisible into two equal parts — that definition covers all even numbers, including the specific even numbers in examples. Similarly, the definition of definition covers all definitions, including itself, without requiring a separate definition. The author then notes a potential flaw: the inclusion is only insofar as it is a definition, not absolutely, but the text cuts off. This is a typical logical subtlety about self-reference and is an important discussion in Ilm al-Mantiq about metadefinitions. An example from Islamic jurisprudence: defining 'hadd' (fixed punishment) as 'a punishment whose measure is determined by Shari'a' would itself be a definition that covers all such punishments, including itself.

تسلسل

Why the Name of a Quiddity Is Not a Definition
Author argues that the name of a thing cannot serve as its definition due to circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why using the name of a quiddity as its definition is circular and fails to meet the conditions of a proper definition.

Core Idea
A name cannot define because it is identical to the thing defined.

In Islamic logic, a definition (hadd) must reveal the unknown quiddity through more known terms. The name of a quiddity (ism al-mahiyya) indicates the quiddity itself, so using it as a definition is circular: the definiendum and definiens are identical. This lesson uncovers the logical flaw and distinguishes naming from real and incomplete definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and proposed definiens
Take any quiddity, like human (insān). The proposed definiens is its name 'insān'. Notice that the definiens is a single word, not a composed statement.
A definition must be a statement (qawl), not a simple term.
2
Apply the condition of being more known
Check if the name is more known than the quiddity. Since the name and the quiddity coincide in meaning, they are equally known. The definiens must be more known than the definiendum, or no knowledge is gained.
The author states: 'a thing is not known by itself, nor by what is more hidden than it.'
3
Recognize circularity (dawr)
If the quiddity is only known through its name, and the name's meaning is the quiddity, then the definition presupposes what it tries to define. This creates a logical loop (dawr).
Circularity invalidates any definition.
4
Distinguish from proper definition and description
Proper definition (hadd haqiqi) uses genus and differentia; description (rasm) uses accidents. Naming does neither, so it fails to be a definition of any kind.
The author explicitly says it is not a real definition, nor incomplete, nor a description.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يخفى فصله عن الرسم وعن الحد الناقص واسم الماهية كـ (اسم الماهية) مثلاً، وإن كان دالاً على كمال الماهية من غير خروج له عن المطابقة والتضمن، إلا أنه مفرد وليس بقول، ولا جرم لم يكن حداً حقيقياً، وإنما لم يكن حداً حقيقياً، بل ولا حداً ناقصاً، بل ولا من جملة الرسوم؛ لأن الحقيقة المجهولة المسؤول عنها كـ (حقيقة (الإنسان مثلاً، إذا كان الجواب الكاشف عنها هو اسمها فمعلوم أن الحد طريق معرف للمجهول، وإنما يكون مُعرفاً إن لو كان ما أخذ أعرف مما يعرف به إذ الشيء لا يعرف بنفسه، ولا بما هو أخفى منه، وليس التعريف بالحد راجعاً إلى نفس اللفظ المأخوذ فيه دون مدلوله، فإنه لو قطع النظر عن مدلول اللفظ لما كان رفاً، وعند ذلك فلا يخفى أن مدلول الاسم المأخوذ هو نفس ما وقع مجهولاً أولاً، والشيء المجهول لا يتوصل إلى معرفته بنفسه، كيف وأن معرفة كون الاسم دالا على الحقيقة المجهولة فرع معرفة الحقيقة فإذا كانت الحقيقة إنمـا تـعـرف بدلالة الاسم عليها كان دوراً ، وتقييدنا له بالماهية المسؤول عنها فاصل له عما ذكر في بيان شرح الاسم، فإنه وإن كان دالاً على كمال الماهية من غير خروج عن دلالة المطابقة والتضمن فليس هو إذ ذاك حداً حقيقياً، إذ الماهية إذ ذاك غير معر ذلك من مسؤول عنها.
And its distinction from description and from the incomplete definition and the name of the quiddity, like (the name of the quiddity) for example, is not hidden. Even if it indicates the perfection of the quiddity without departing from correspondence and implication, still it is simple and not a statement, and consequently it is not a real definition. Rather it is not a real definition, nor even an incomplete definition, nor from the set of descriptions; because the unknown quiddity asked about, like (the quiddity of man) for example, if the revealing answer is its name, then it is known that definition is a path to knowledge of the unknown, and it becomes a definer only if what is taken is more known than what is defined by it, for a thing is not known by itself, nor by what is more hidden than it. And definition by definition does not refer to the very word taken in it without its meaning, for if one disregards the meaning of the word, it would not be a definer. At that point, it is clear that the meaning of the name taken is exactly what was unknown initially, and the unknown thing cannot be arrived at by itself. How so, while knowledge that the name indicates the unknown quiddity is branch upon knowledge of the quiddity; if the quiddity is known only by the indication of the name upon it, it would be circular. And our restriction of it to the quiddity asked about distinguishes it from what was mentioned in explanation of the name, for even if it indicates the perfection of the quiddity without departing from the indication of correspondence and implication, it is then not a real definition, since the quiddity then is not known [by that] from what is asked about.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage defines the distinction between a true definition (hadd haqiqi) and merely stating the name of a quiddity (ism al-mahiyya). The author argues that giving the name of a thing as its definition is invalid because it would be circular: the name's meaning is identical to the quiddity itself, so the definiendum and definiens are the same, and a thing cannot be known by itself. In Islamic logic, a definition must be composed of more known terms (genus and differentia) to reveal the unknown. For example, defining 'insan' (human) as 'hayawan natiq' (rational animal) is a proper definition because 'animal' and 'rational' are more known than 'human'. Saying 'insan is insan' gives no new knowledge. The text also distinguishes between a real definition, an incomplete definition (had naqis), and a description (rasm), emphasizing that mere naming fails all these categories.

Key Terms
حد
رسم
اسم الماهية
دور

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because it is a single word, not a composed statement.
B) Because it indicates the quiddity by correspondence and implication.
C) Because it is more known than the quiddity.
D) Because it uses accidents rather than essence.

Key Takeaway
A definition must be composed of terms more known than the definiendum; using the mere name is circular and fails to provide knowledge.

Levels of Definition and Refuting Infinite Regress
Author distinguishes between hadd, hadd al-hadd, and hadd hadd al-hadd, refuting infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hadd, hadd al-hadd, and hadd hadd al-hadd, and explain why the infinite regress objection fails.

Core Idea
The definition of a definition is not the definition itself; meta-levels are distinct but not infinite.

This passage explores the layered nature of definitions: the definition of a thing, the definition of that definition, and so on. You might worry that this leads to an infinite regress, but the author shows it is only potential. Understanding these levels is crucial for precise logical discourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three levels
Find in the text the three distinct levels: hadd (definition of a thing), hadd al-hadd (definition of definition), and hadd hadd al-hadd (definition of the definition of definition). Notice how each is defined.
The author uses 'man' as an example: hadd = rational animal; hadd al-hadd = statement indicating what makes that definition correct.
2
Understand specificity at each level
See that while all three share the generic 'definition', each has a specific meaning that the generic does not capture. The definition of man is not the definition of the definition of man.
3
Analyze the infinite regress objection
The author mentions that this chain could go to infinity, but he refutes it by distinguishing potential from actual. We do not need to actually define every level; we stop where convenient.
The objection is that defining definition forces an endless chain; the author says only potential regress exists, not actual.
4
Evaluate the brevity condition
The author rejects brevity (ijaz) as a condition because it is relative. What is concise for one may be verbose for another, so it cannot be part of a fixed definition.
This shows the importance of objective criteria in definitions.

الفصل الأول: في بيان ما هو النافع من المركبات في تحصيل المطلوبات الحد مماثل في الحقيقة لحد الحد من حيث هو حد، وليس ذلك مغنياً عن من حيث هو حد حد الحد، فإنه من هذه الجهة مخالف لحد الحد، إذ حد الحد بالفعل هو القول الدال على ماهية الحد أو تصوره، وحد حد الحد وإن دخل تحت حد الحد من حيث هو حد، فليس بداخل تحته من جهة خصوصيته، وهو كونه دالاً على حد حد الحد، كما أن حد الإنسان هو الحيوان الناطق، وهو وإن دخل تحت مطلق الحد من حيث هو حد فليس بداخل تحته من جهة خصوصيته، وهو كونه حد الإنسان إذ مطلق الحد لا يعرب عنه، وإن أعرب عنه من حيث هو حد ما، كيف وإن حد شيء ما لا يكون هو نفس حد ذلك الشيء، فإن حد الإنسان إنه حيوان ناطق وليس حد حده أنه حيوان ناطق بل قول دال على ما به يكون الإنسان هو هو، وكذا ليس حد هذا الحد هو نفسه بل القول الدال على ما به يكون القول الدال على ماهية الإنسان هو هو، وكذا حد الحد بالفعل هو القول الدال على ما به يكون الحد هو هو، وحد حد الحد هو القول الدال على ما به يكون القول الدال على ماهية الحد هو هو، وجميع هذه الحدود وإن اشتركت في معنى مطلق الحد فليس البعض معرباً عن خصوصيته ما للبعض الآخر، بل لكل واحد حد بخصوصيته، وهو مغاير لحد الآخر.
وهذا وإن ذهب إلى غير النهاية كما ذكروه، ولكن لا بمعنى أنه مهما ذكرنا حد الحد بالفعل فيلزمنا ذكر حد حده وحـد حـده بالفعل إلى غير النهاية إذ ليس يلزم من ذكر حد بعض الأشياء ذكر حد كل الأشياء، بل منها ما يسهل فنذكره، ومنها ما يصعب فنهمله، وربما أهملناه مع سهولته، ولا بمعنى أنه مهما ذكر حد بعض الأشياء بالفعل فقد ذكر حد جميعها بالفعل، بل الموجود بالفعل ليس إلا ما ذكر، وإنما ذلك بالقوة وليس من تسليم التسلسل في ذلك وعدم النهاية فيه محال، ولا التفات إلى من يشترط الإيجاز في الحد حتى قال في حده إنه قول وجيز يدل على الماهية المطلوبة، إذ الوجيز معنى إضافي وهو غير منضبط، إذ ما من وجيز بالنسبة إلى شيء إلا وهو مطوّل بالنسبة إلى غيره، فلا يمكن أخذه في الحد.
Chapter One: On explaining what is beneficial among composites for attaining desired things. The definition is similar in reality to the definition of definition (hadd al-hadd) insofar as it is a definition, but that does not suffice for [defining] the definition of definition (hadd hadd al-hadd) insofar as it is a definition of definition, for from this perspective it is different from the definition of definition. Indeed, the actual definition of definition (hadd al-hadd bil-fi'l) is the statement indicating the quiddity of definition or its conceptualization. The definition of the definition of definition, though it falls under the definition of definition insofar as it is a definition, does not fall under it from the perspective of its specificity, namely its being indicative of the definition of the definition of definition. Just as the definition of man is 'rational animal', and though it falls under absolute definition insofar as it is a definition, it does not fall under it from the perspective of its specificity, namely its being the definition of man, for absolute definition does not express it, even if it expresses it insofar as it is some definition. Indeed, the definition of a thing is not identical to the definition of that thing's definition. For the definition of man is 'rational animal', and the definition of its definition is not 'rational animal' but a statement indicating that by which man is what he is. Likewise, the definition of this definition is not itself but the statement indicating that by which the statement indicating the quiddity of man is what it is. Likewise, the actual definition of definition is the statement indicating that by which definition is what it is, and the definition of the definition of definition is the statement indicating that by which the statement indicating the quiddity of definition is what it is. All these definitions, though they share in the meaning of absolute definition, one is not expressive of the specificity of another. Rather, each has its own definition specific to it, which is different from the definition of the other.
Now, this [chain] goes on to infinity as they mentioned, but not in the sense that whenever we mention the actual definition of definition we must then mention the definition of its definition, and so on to infinity, for mentioning the definition of some things does not necessitate mentioning the definition of all things. Rather, some are easy and we mention them, some are difficult and we omit them, and sometimes we omit them even if easy. Nor does it mean that whenever we mention the actual definition of some things we have actually mentioned the definition of all of them. Rather, what actually exists is only what is mentioned; the rest is only potential. Acknowledging an infinite regress here is not required, and infinity is impossible. No attention is paid to those who require brevity in definition, to the extent that they said in its definition that it is a concise statement indicating the desired quiddity, for concise is a relative meaning that is not well-defined. Indeed, no concise thing in relation to something is but it is verbose in relation to something else, so it cannot be taken in definition.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the concept of definition and its meta-definitions. The author begins by distinguishing between three levels: the definition of a thing (hadd), the definition of definition (hadd al-hadd), and the definition of the definition of definition (hadd hadd al-hadd). He argues that while all share the generic concept of definition, each has its own specific meaning. For example, the definition of man is 'rational animal', but the definition of that definition is not 'rational animal' but rather a statement describing what makes that definition correct. The author then addresses the objection that this leads to an infinite regress. He refutes it by explaining that the sequence is only potential, not actual: we do not need to define every meta-definition; we only define those that are convenient. Finally, he rejects the condition of brevity (ijaz) in definitions, arguing that brevity is relative and cannot be objectively determined. This lesson teaches the precision required in logical definitions and the pitfalls of infinite regress.

The Method of Complete Real Definition: Nearest Genus and Differentia
Author explains how to form a complete real definition using nearest genus and differentia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a complete real definition (hadd tamm haqiqi) for any given term by identifying its nearest genus and specific differentia.

Core Idea
A complete definition needs only the nearest genus and the differentia, not every essential attribute.

In the previous lesson, you learned what a complete real definition is. Now, the author explains the practical method for constructing one. The key is to use the nearest genus and the specific differentia, because the nearest genus automatically includes all higher genera. This lesson will guide you through this method and show why listing every essential attribute individually is unnecessary and even discouraged in the art of definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term to be defined
Find the definiendum (e.g., 'man'). Determine its essential attributes (dhatiyyat).
2
Find the nearest genus
What is the most immediate genus that includes the term? For man, it is 'animal'. If the genus has no name, define it.
The nearest genus implicitly includes all higher genera (substance, body, etc.).
3
Find the specific differentia
What distinguishes the term from other species under the same genus? For man, it is 'rational'.
The differentia does not imply the genus; it must be explicitly stated.
4
Combine genus and differentia to form the definition
The complete real definition is 'rational animal'. This suffices to capture the full quiddity because the genus contains higher genera.
Listing all essential attributes individually is redundant and disliked in the art of definition.
5
Check for completeness
Ensure that the definition includes both common and specific essential attributes. Avoid incomplete definitions that omit genera or differentiae.
Differentiae alone do not indicate the genus; they only imply it through concomitance, which is insufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذ عرفت ما لخصناه في تعريف الحد التام الحقيقي، فذلك إنما يتم بذكر جميع الذاتيات العامة للشيء المحدود والخاصة له ولو كانت ألفاً، لكن الطريق الخاصي في ذلك إن كانت الذاتيات أجناساً وفصولاً أن يذكر أولاً ما هو أقرب الأجناس إلى الشيء المحدد، إما باسمه إن كان له اسم، أو بحده إن لم يكن له اسم ثم يقرن به ما له من الفصول، فإن الجنس القريب يتضمن ما فوقه من الذاتيات العامة، فإذا قرن به ما له من الفصول فقد تمت الماهية وذلك كما يقال في حد الإنسان مثلاً إنه حيوان ناطق أو جسم، ذو نفس ،حساس، ناطق أن لو قدر أنه لا اسم للحيوان فإن أقرب الأجناس إليه إنما هو الحيوان ويتضمن ما فوقه من الجوهر والجسم وذي النفس وغير ذلك، وما له من الفصول ليس إلا الناطق، فهذا الحد التام الحقيقي المذكور على النمط الخاصي.
جميع لو رُمت أن نذكر ما له من الذاتيات كل واحد بطريق المطابقة، بأن نقول مثلاً في حد الإنسان أنه جوهر متجسم ذو ،نفس ،نام حساس، ناطق، أو نذكر بدل اسم الجنس القريب حده مع تمكنك من ذكر اسمه كان مكروهاً بالنظر إلى الصنعة الحدّيّة؛ لحصول المقصود دونه، ولكن لا يختل به الحد.
والعبرة عن الحقيقة المقصودة على ما حققناه لو اقتصر من ذكر الذاتيات العامة على بعضها، أو من فصول إن كان له فصول على بعضها، أو على الأجناس وحدها، أو الفصول وحدها، لم يكن القول دالاً على كمال الماهية؛ لأن الفصول بعضها إن حصل به التمييز فليس لها دلالة على ما للشيء من الذاتيات العامة إلا بطريق الالتزام ولا اعتبار بها في الحدود الحقيقية التامة، وذلك كمال في دلالة الناطق على الحيوان، إذ الحيوان ليس هو نفس مدلول الناطق، ولا داخلاً في معناه، بل الناطق شيء ذو نطق اتفق إن كان حيواناً، ومـن فـشـر النـاطق بذي النفس الناطقة، والنفس بكمال أوّل لجسم طبيعي الذي لم يلزم أن يكون الفصل متضمناً للجسم والحيوان، إذ الفصل إنما هو ذات النفس لا بما عرض لها من كونها كمالاً للجسم، وهي لا تتضمن الجسم، بل ولا دلالة لبعض الفصول
And when you have understood what we summarized concerning the definition of the complete real definition, that is only completed by mentioning all the common essential attributes (dhatiyyat) of the thing defined and the specific ones, even if they were a thousand. However, the specific method for that, if the essential attributes are genera and differentiae, is to first mention the nearest genus to the thing defined, either by its name if it has a name, or by its definition if it has no name, then to conjoin with it its differentiae. For the nearest genus includes the common essential attributes above it, so when its differentiae are conjoined with it, the quiddity is complete. For example, in defining man one says 'rational animal' or 'body, ensouled, sensitive, rational' if one supposes that there is no name for 'animal'. The nearest genus to it is 'animal', which includes what is above it like 'substance', 'body', 'ensouled', etc., and its differentia is only 'rational'. So this is the complete real definition mentioned according to the specific pattern.
All [this is] if you wish to mention all its essential attributes each by way of correspondence (mutabaqa), as when we say in defining man 'substance, embodied, ensouled, growing, sensitive, rational', or instead of the name of the nearest genus we mention its definition while you are able to mention its name, it would be disliked from the perspective of the art of definition, because the purpose is achieved without it, but the definition is not invalidated thereby.
The consideration of the intended reality is as we have verified: if one restricts [the mention] of the common essential attributes to some of them, or of the differentiae (if there are differentiae) to some of them, or to the genera alone, or the differentiae alone, the statement would not be indicative of the full quiddity. For the differentiae, even if some of them achieve distinction, they do not indicate what the thing has of common essential attributes except via implication (iltizam), and that is not considered in complete real definitions. For example, the indication of 'rational' for 'animal': 'animal' is not the same as the meaning of 'rational', nor is it included in its meaning; rather, 'rational' is something possessing rationality that happens to be an animal. And whoever interprets 'rational' as 'possessing a rational soul', and the soul as 'the first perfection of a natural body', it does not entail that the differentia includes body and animal. For the differentia is the essence of the soul, not incidental attributes like being a perfection of the body, and it does not include the body. In fact, some differentiae do not indicate [the higher genera] at all.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage explains the proper method for constructing a complete real definition (al-hadd al-tamm al-haqiqi). The author begins by stating that ideally, a complete definition should list all essential attributes (dhatiyyat), both common and specific. However, the practical method recommended is to mention only the nearest genus and the specific differentia. The nearest genus implicitly includes all higher genera, so there is no need to list them separately. The author illustrates with the definition of man: 'rational animal' suffices because 'animal' contains 'body', 'substance', etc. If one were to list all essential attributes individually (e.g., 'substance, body, ensouled, sensitive, rational'), it would be permissible but considered redundant in the art of definition. The passage then addresses the problem of insufficient definitions: if one omits some essential attributes or mentions only genera or only differentiae, the definition fails to capture the full quiddity. The author explains that differentiae like 'rational' do not imply the higher genera directly; they only indicate them by implication (iltizam), which is not sufficient for a complete real definition. The example of interpreting 'rational' as 'possessing a rational soul' shows that the differentia does not necessarily include body or animal. This highlights the importance of a proper definition that explicitly includes the genus and differentia.

Method of Complete Real Definition: Nearest Genus and Differentia
Author explains the proper method of forming a complete real definition by starting with the closest genus then adding differentia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a complete real definition for any term by identifying its nearest genus and adding the correct differentia, using examples from Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Efficient definitions start with the closest genus, which carries all higher genera.

In the previous lesson, you learned what a complete real definition is. Now the author teaches the efficient method: begin with the nearest genus, then add the differentia. This saves time and captures the essence fully. For example, defining man as 'animal, rational' works because 'animal' already implies substance, body, etc. Let's see how this method applies in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term to be defined
Choose the definiendum. For example, 'human' or 'wine' in fiqh. Ensure it is a species or a thing with a quiddity.
2
Find the nearest genus
Look for the immediate broader category. For human, it's 'animal'. For wine, it might be 'intoxicating beverage' if that is a genus. If the genus has no name, define it first.
The nearest genus includes all higher genera implicitly.
3
Add the differentia
Determine what distinguishes the species from other members of that genus. For human, it's rationality (al-natiq). For wine, it's 'intoxicating' or 'fermented from grapes' depending on the definition.
The differentia is the specific essential attribute.
4
Check completeness
Ensure the definition includes all essential attributes. Since the nearest genus contains higher genera, listing only the nearest genus and differentia is sufficient for a complete real definition.
Example: 'animal, rational' captures all essential attributes of human.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذ عرفت ما لخصناه في تعريف الحد التام الحقيقي، فذلك إنما يتم بذكر جميع الذاتيات العامة للشيء المحدود والخاصة له ولو كانت ألفاً، لكن الطريق الخاصي في ذلك إن كانت الذاتيات أجناساً وفصولاً أن يذكر أولاً ما هو أقرب الأجناس إلى الشيء المحدد، إما باسمه إن كان له اسم، أو بحده إن لم يكن له اسم ثم يقرن به ما له من الفصول، فإن الجنس القريب يتضمن ما فوقه من الذاتيات العامة، فإذا قرن به ما له من الفصول فقد تمت الماهية وذلك كما يقال في حد الإنسان مثلاً إنه حيوان ناطق أو جسم، ذو نفس، حساس، ناطق أن لو قدر أنه لا اسم للحيوان فإن أقرب الأجناس إليه إنما هو الحيوان ويتضمن ما فوقه من الجوهر والجسم وذي النفس وغير ذلك، وما له من الفصول ليس إلا الناطق، فهذا الحد التام الحقيقي المذكور على النمط الخاصي.
And when you know what we have summarized in the definition of the complete real definition, that is only accomplished by mentioning all the general essential attributes of the defined thing and its specific ones, even if they were a thousand. But the special way in that, if the essential attributes are genera and species, is to mention first the nearest genus to the defined thing, either by its name if it has a name, or by its definition if it does not have a name, then to couple with it whatever species it has. For the nearest genus includes what is above it from the general essential attributes, so when one couples with it whatever species it has, the quiddity is completed. And that is as is said in the definition of man, for example: 'animal, rational' or 'body, possessing a soul, sensory, rational' if it is supposed that there is no name for animal. For the nearest genus to him is only 'animal', and it includes what is above it of substance, body, possessor of soul, and other things. And what he has of species is only 'rational'. So this is the complete real definition mentioned in the special manner.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage defines the proper method for constructing a complete real definition (al-hadd al-tam al-haqiqi). The author states that such a definition requires mentioning all the essential attributes (dhatiyat) of the thing, both general and specific. However, he points out that the efficient and special way (al-tariq al-khasi) is to start with the nearest genus (aqrab al-ajnas) and then add the differentia (fasl). The nearest genus implicitly contains all the higher genera. For example, in defining 'human', one can say 'animal, rational' because 'animal' already implies substance, body, etc. If the genus has no name, one may use its definition. The passage emphasizes that this method captures the full quiddity without listing every single essential attribute individually.

Why a Definition Must Include All Essential Attributes
Author argues that omitting any essential attribute fails to express the complete quiddity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why omitting either the genus or differentia invalidates a definition according to the three types of indication (mutabaqa, tadamun, iltizam).

Core Idea
In complete real definitions, each essential attribute must be indicated directly, not merely by implication.

This passage explains why a definition must express the complete quiddity. The author argues that if only some attributes are mentioned, the definition fails because the missing attributes are only implied, not directly indicated. Understanding the three modes of indication—application (mutabaqa), inclusion (tadamun), and implication (iltizam)—is crucial for evaluating definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three modes of indication
Recall that terms can indicate meanings in three ways: al-mutabaqa (direct correspondence), al-tadamun (inclusion of a part), and al-iltizam (implication of something else). The passage emphasizes that for definitions, only the first two are acceptable for expressing the complete quiddity.
These terms are technical; review the key terms if needed.
2
Understand why a single differentia is insufficient
Consider the example of 'rational' (al-natiq) as a differentia for 'animal' (al-hayawan). 'Rational' does not directly convey 'animal' by application or inclusion; it only implies it. The author argues that such implication is not accepted in complete real definitions.
The differentia distinguishes but does not directly indicate the genus.
3
Recognize that implication (iltizam) is not sufficient
The passage states that implication is not considered in complete real definitions. Even though 'rational' necessarily implies 'animal', that implication alone does not make the definition complete. The definition must explicitly include the genus.
4
Apply the insight to a definition
Given a definition like 'human is rational', identify that it lacks the genus 'animal' directly. Check if each essential attribute (genus and differentia) is indicated by mutabaqa or tadamun. If any attribute is only implied, the definition is incomplete.
This is the core test for completeness of real definitions (hadd haqiqi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعبرة عن الحقيقة المقصودة على ما حققناه لو اقتصر من ذكر الذاتيات العامة على بعضها، أو من فصول إن كان له فصول على بعضها، أو على الأجناس وحدها، أو الفصول وحدها، لم يكن القول دالاً على كمال الماهية؛ لأن الفصول بعضها إن حصل به التمييز فليس لها دلالة على ما للشيء من الذاتيات العامة إلا بطريق الالتزام ولا اعتبار بها في الحدود الحقيقية التامة، وذلك كمال في دلالة الناطق على الحيوان، إذ الحيوان ليس هو نفس مدلول الناطق، ولا داخلاً في معناه، بل الناطق شيء ذو نطق اتفق إن كان حيواناً، ومن تفسير الناطق بذي النفس الناطقة، والنفس بكمال أول لجسم طبيعي الذي لا يلزم أن يكون الفصل متضمناً للجسم والحيوان، إذ الفصل إنما هو ذات النفس لا بما عرض لها من كونها كمالاً للجسم، وهي لا تتضمن الجسم، بل ولا دلالة لبعض الفصول على بعض أيضاً، إلا بطريق الالتزام كما في الحساس، والمتحرك بالإرادة، للحيوان، ولا اعتبار به في الحد الحقيقي التام، وأما الذاتيات العامة فإنها لا تدل على ما تحتها مما هو أخص منها، كان ذلك عاماً بالنسبة إلى الشيء المحدود أو خاصاً لا بطريق المطابقة ولا التضمن ولا بالالتزام، فالاقتصار عليها أو على بعضها لا يكون مفيدا.
And the consideration of the intended reality according to what we have verified: if one restricts himself to mentioning some of the general essential attributes, or some of the species if it has species, or to the genera alone, or the species alone, the statement would not indicate the completeness of the quiddity. Because some species, even if they achieve distinction, do not indicate what the thing has of general essential attributes except by way of implication, and such implication is not considered in complete real definitions. That is perfect in the indication of 'rational' for 'animal', for 'animal' is not the same as the meaning of 'rational', nor is it included in its meaning. Rather, 'rational' is something possessing reason that happens to be an animal. And from the explanation of 'rational' as 'possessor of rational soul', and the soul is the first perfection of a natural body, it does not necessitate that the differentia include body and animal. For the differentia is only the soul itself, not by virtue of its being a perfection of the body, and it does not include the body. Moreover, some species do not indicate others either, except by way of implication, as in 'sensitive' and 'voluntarily moving' for 'animal'. And such implication is not considered in the complete real definition. As for the general essential attributes, they do not indicate what is below them that is more specific, whether that is general relative to the defined thing or specific, neither by application nor by inclusion nor by implication. So restricting oneself to them or to some of them is not beneficial.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage explains why a definition must include both general and specific essential attributes. The author argues that if one mentions only some of the general attributes or only the differentia, the definition fails to indicate the complete quiddity. The reason is that a differentia alone, though it distinguishes, does not imply the genus except by way of implication (iltizam), and such implication is not considered valid in complete real definitions. For example, 'rational' does not directly convey 'animal'; it only implies it incidentally. The author further clarifies that neither do differentia imply each other directly. And general essential attributes do not indicate their subordinates either by mutabaqa (application), tadamun (inclusion), or iltizam (implication). Therefore, any omission renders the definition insufficient.

الالتزام
المطابقة
التضمن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a single differentia insufficient for a complete real definition according to this passage?
A) Because it does not distinguish the defined thing.
B) Because it does not indicate the genus by application or inclusion.
C) Because it is too specific.
D) Because it requires the name of the genus.

Key Takeaway
A complete real definition must directly indicate both the genus and the differentia by application or inclusion, not merely by implication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition of 'salat' as 'specific statements and actions, beginning with takbir and ending with taslim, performed with intention.' Identify which parts are the genus and differentia. Is the genus directly stated or only implied? Evaluate whether this definition is complete according to the criteria from the passage.
?
Construct a complete real definition for 'zakat' using essential attributes. Verify that both the genus (e.g., charity/sadaqah) and differentia (e.g., obligatory, specific conditions) are indicated by application or inclusion, not merely implication.
